  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6db28f31-f1e3-40e4-9f1e-33d2187db34a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText5213889082601016805" style="display:none">When "Perfect" Parker Fadley starts drinking at school and failing her classes, all of St. Peter's High goes on alert. How has the cheerleading captain, girlfriend of the most popular guy in school, consummate teacher's pet, and future valedictorian fallen so far from grace?<br /><br />Parker doesn't want to talk about it. She'd just like to be left alone, to disappear, to be ignored. But her parents have placed her on suicide watch and her conselors are demanding the truth. Worse, there's a nice guy falling in love with her and he's making her feel things again when she'd really rather not be feeling anything at all.<br /><br />Nobody would have guessed she'd turn out like this. But nobody knows the truth.<br /><br />Something horrible has happened, and it just might be her fault.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/934682-how-did-jessie-die-it-s-never-specified"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[How did Jessie die? It's never specified. Are we to assume she killed herself? If the guy who raped her killed her, wouldn't that have been reported to the police? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<ul class='questionFooterActions'>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_934682'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F45046784-cracked-up-to-be">like</a></span>

</li>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/934682-how-did-jessie-die-it-s-never-specified">Add your answer</a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/37914925-kira"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1419399562i/37914925._UY100_CR3,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/37914925-kira">Kira</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    The assumption is the guy who raped her killed her. The last time Parker saw him, he was taking Jessie further into the woods. Jessie had told others <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    The assumption is the guy who raped her killed her. The last time Parker saw him, he was taking Jessie further into the woods. Jessie had told others that she was going to run away, and no one except Parker knew Jessie had been in the woods. Therefore the police had no reason to look for her in the woods. I'm not sure of the time period, but it was at least six months, perhaps a year, before Jessie's body was found. There might have been some DNA evidence still remaining, but it is doubtful. Even if there was, it would have to be matched with the killer, and if he hadn't done anything else - or hadn't been caught - his DNA wouldn't be in the system. So the chances of his being caught were slim.<br /><br />As for reporting the rape, that is the entire point of the book - Parker did not report it, either that night or the next day after she sobered up. It is not clear why she didn't, except that she felt guilty for telling Jessie about Evan's infidelity, therefore leading Jessie to break up with him and go looking for someone else, ultimately leading to her rape and death. Guilt (IMO) is not a good enough reason not to call 911 when you see someone being raped.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1639303443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1241451334388343424"><br/>Every time I finish a book by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers' title='Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Courtney Summers</a>, all my brain seems to want to do is <strong>ponder the meaning of life</strong>.<br/><br/>It’s not even that her books are philosophical, but they’re just so raw that I feel emotionally connected to everything, and when I get to the last page, it all comes to a stop.<br/><br/><strong>Except it doesn’t</strong>, because then I want to crawl back into the book and decorticate the main character some more. And I relate her to myself. And then I relate myself to the world. And then I relate the world to l</span>
  <span id="freeText1241451334388343424" style="display:none"><br />Every time I finish a book by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a>, all my brain seems to want to do is <strong>ponder the meaning of life</strong>.<br /><br />It’s not even that her books are philosophical, but they’re just so raw that I feel emotionally connected to everything, and when I get to the last page, it all comes to a stop.<br /><br /><strong>Except it doesn’t</strong>, because then I want to crawl back into the book and decorticate the main character some more. And I relate her to myself. And then I relate myself to the world. And then I relate the world to life.<br /><br />It’s a peculiar longish procedure, which is why I don’t read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a>’ works all that often. Not that she has tons of novels written.<br /><br />Why doesn’t she have tons of novels written? She sure has the talent and imagination necessary and I especially like how she doesn’t write what most people love reading about.<br /><br />For instance, Parker – the heroine – is messed up. She did something bad, and she thinks she has to pay for it by sweeping everyone out of her life. One by one. She wants to be left alone, wallowing in her misery.<br /><br />She’s mean. She’s unpleasantly honest. And she’s unreliable. She’ll make us think that we know her, but the truth is we don’t. Even <em>she</em> isn’t always sure what she wants. <strong>I love these types of characters so much.</strong><br /><br /><strong> </strong>A teacher I once had told us that the best characters we’ll come across in literature will be imperfect. She said those are the ones readers will be able to connect with. You know why. Because we’re imperfect, yet we still seek perfection.<br /><br />Just ask Parker, she knows all about it. She used to be popular, heard-of-class and strikingly good at everything. A perfectionist. Before she fell apart.<br /><br />What I also like about Summers’ books is how she never tries to overwhelm us. She paces her novels well and never adds the kind of thick atmosphere that will make us feel uncomfortable or unable to breathe.<br /><br />Her novels are strangely quiet. It’s all calm… until it isn’t anymore… and then it’s calm again. <strong>Like the sea. </strong>But the themes are always so powerful that sometimes we’re scared we’re not going to be able to get them out of our minds.<br /><br /><strong>Sigh… I just… can’t recommend this author enough.</strong><br /><br /><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=lolareviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">BD</a> | <a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1241451334388343424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3155997822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3155997822" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3155997822?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3155997822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15149239459475629479">After reading “Sadie” and became speechless, numb, screaming for two days in pain, I learned from the experience, this author is a shining gem at the literature’s treasure box! And I promise myself everything Courtney Summer writes even they’re shopping list, ridiculous post it notes, greeting cards or restriction order against me for being half witted fan, I’m going to write them without questioning!<br/><br/> As soon as I heard this book’s republishing, instead of reading the previous works (yes my tbr </span>
  <span id="freeText15149239459475629479" style="display:none">After reading “Sadie” and became speechless, numb, screaming for two days in pain, I learned from the experience, this author is a shining gem at the literature’s treasure box! And I promise myself everything Courtney Summer writes even they’re shopping list, ridiculous post it notes, greeting cards or restriction order against me for being half witted fan, I’m going to write them without questioning!<br /><br /> As soon as I heard this book’s republishing, instead of reading the previous works (yes my tbr list already threatens me to explode into my face any second and it’s getting fatter than my husband’s belly reminds you of an elephant’s belly after eating his girlfriend.) of writer including “All the Rage” (I swear I’ll read next week! I’m telling same thing every week and another Arc copy hits on my face and distracts my attention!) and “This is not a test”<br /><br />So when I saw this book’s arc copy on the Netflix, I clicked the request button, feeling myself like a Voice judge, turning her chair at the blind audition. As soon as I saw it on my library, I began my salsa moves and in the mean time I dived into without waiting any further. <br /><br />It was fast pacing, intriguing, interesting and brilliantly written book. I should give it 3.5 stars and round them up! Wait! What! If I love the writing, why am I cutting points? What the hell is wrong with me?<br /><br />Wrong question! I wanted to ask the same one to the anti-heroine Parker Fadley from the beginning of the book. I wanted to say: “Hey, you self-absorbed, mean, manipulative, lying, shameless bitch! Why are you acting like that? Why are you self-sabotaging yourself by alienating your friends, your family?” She didn’t treat well to her new dog, which made me more pissed off and I wish I could jump into the book and slap her several times and come back after getting my hate out of my system!<br /><br />Parker was shining star of her high school before she goes nuts and turning her life into a mess. She was cheerleader captain (she quit), Chris, most popular guy of the school’s girlfriend (stole his money and broke up with him), future valedictorian ( now she steals her friends’ essays and copies them)! Something is really really really wrong with her but she denies to talk about even though everyone tolerates her antics and remains patient with her.<br /> <br />The author chose to create a heroine WE PASSIONATELY LOVE TO HATE HER! But we were hooked from the first page because we understood that something happened at Chris’ party and Parker’s close friend Jessie disappeared at that night. Parker keeps a big secret and she keeps treating the people around her like hell to try helping her. Especially new guy Jake who recently transferred to their school turns into a punch bag of her (Oh Parker, you gave me so much reason to drag you throughout the school halls by pulling your hair!) So you keep telling yourself! WHAT THE HELL IS WRONG WITH HER?<br /> <br />The author’s tricky story-telling for giving us some quick glimpses and special sneak peeks from the night is the smartest way to keep our attention intact. We want to know the reasons, we want to know where the hell Jessie is and we want to know how far this crazy bitch Parker can go for self-destruction!<br />And BAMMM we got the answers. The ending is realistic, satisfying but not so much emotional or heart wrenching as I expected. And yes, I understand Parker’s motives but I still cannot empathize with her. <br /> <br />Overall: It was realistic, questioning, unconventional, riveting reading even though there are too many characters with unlikeable behaviors and too much flaws. It was a great, fast YA fiction book. Not my favorite Courtney Summers book but it’s still so much better from too many books I’ve read from the same genre.<br /><br />Special thanks to NetGalley and St. Martin’sPress/Wednesday Books for sharing this fantastic ARC COPY with me in exchange my honest review.</span>

<div id="review_3168140988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3168140988" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3168140988?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2550422-st-martin-s-press">St. Martin&#39;s Press</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=bookstagram-made-me-do-it">bookstagram-made-me-do-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3168140988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17603415959350394061">It's fair to note that I'm an adult, and therefore NOT the target audience for this book, but I whole-heartedly believe that <i>Cracked Up to Be</i> is the book I needed as a teen. Also noting that this is a re-release of a novel first published in 2008, I found it incredible in the sense that it's thematic issues transferred over to the present time flawlessly, although this partially could be due to some updates in the content to bring the story into the current decade's level of technology. All that</span>
  <span id="freeText17603415959350394061" style="display:none">It's fair to note that I'm an adult, and therefore NOT the target audience for this book, but I whole-heartedly believe that <i>Cracked Up to Be</i> is the book I needed as a teen. Also noting that this is a re-release of a novel first published in 2008, I found it incredible in the sense that it's thematic issues transferred over to the present time flawlessly, although this partially could be due to some updates in the content to bring the story into the current decade's level of technology. All that to say, I'm not a young adult anymore, but as a mother of two young girls, YA contemporaries featuring the struggles my daughters might encounter one day interest me. My oldest will be a teenager in just 6 short years, and while that seems like an eternity on glance, I'm pretty other parents here will understand just how fleeting each precious second is with our children.<br /><br />Parker Fadley is an intentionally unlikeable character. That's not a cheap shot at the story, as the author herself states this fact in the introduction to the book. Parker tries incredibly hard to distance herself from everyone she knows and cares for, due to a careless mistake she committed in her junior year of high school. Most of the story is told in the present, after the event, but the suspense builds throughout as we slowly get flashback glances into how the night in question unfolded. Part of what makes this book so powerful is not that the author pulls every outrageous twist in her arsenal, or makes every single teenage issue happen to Parker herself, but she does touch on a lot of the tough content inserted into teen fiction these days, such as rape, suicide, and a brief mention of abortions that are not part of the narrative. <br /><br />Truly, this is a story about Perfect Parker and what happens to her when this facade is forcibly removed. While I do think that all the adults are portrayed as complete idiots in this book, I think it's fair to assume that the book is written in an accurate way due to the fact that the author was only 22 when the book was published. I appreciate that, while all adults are not completely tuned out to when a kid is in trouble, this story does a great job of showing what it might feel like through the eyes of a teenager in that moment, and also how, while we want to help every kid that we see struggling, we might have no idea as adults in the best way to reach them. Mental health is really the theme that this story circles around, and I truly appreciate how the book ends on a messy, but hopeful note. Nothing is tied up in a pretty little bow, and this felt so authentic and real that I wanted to give Parker a standing ovation. If you're looking for a lightning fast read where the suspense of "what happened" will keep you turning the pages, please give <i>Cracked Up to Be</i> a try. <br /><br /><i>*Many thanks to the publisher for providing my review copy.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17603415959350394061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1205329857" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1205329857" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1205329857?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1205329857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16026982712082153904"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461850639i/18919301._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>☠ <b>
  <u>Warning</u>
</b> : I thought about it over and over, and the only way I feel writing this review includes a great amount of personal information. If you don't care about it, if you think that's not a review, if you - well, just thought I'd warn you. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"You know how when you meet someone and they just give you the impression they're living on this entirely different planet from everyone else? That's sort of how I felt when I met you."</b>
</blockquote><br/>I don't really know what to say. I mean, how am I supposed to sa</span>
  <span id="freeText16026982712082153904" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461850639i/18919301._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>☠ <b>
  <u>Warning</u>
</b> : I thought about it over and over, and the only way I feel writing this review includes a great amount of personal information. If you don't care about it, if you think that's not a review, if you - well, just thought I'd warn you. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You know how when you meet someone and they just give you the impression they're living on this entirely different planet from everyone else? That's sort of how I felt when I met you."</b>
</blockquote><br>I don't really know what to say. I mean, how am I supposed to say that I can <i>relate</i> to Parker without sounding like a bitch? Because I do, but I'm not, and I wasn't. Lost a little? I'll explain. The fact is, above her actions, what stroke me the most in Parker was her need to be herself, even if the way she chose to do so appeared to be incredibly harsh and selfish at times. <br><br>What I love in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> is the way she manages to take the high-school stereotypes and to go <i>further</i>, <b>to crack the shells in order to show what's hidden beneath all the craps we're served in so many young adult books</b>. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You've made a choice and it's so obvious. I see it; I accept it," she says. "Even if no one else can. You want to rot and I want to let you."</b>
</blockquote><br>If I struggled more with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10435892.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a>, that's because I found it more difficult to imagine the situation there and I know that I'm in the minority about this. But the truth is, if I never saw groups of people behaving like these assholes in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10435892.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a>, <b>Parker sounds real to me, and yes, I can relate</b>. If I was never mean to people like she can be, I went through a tough phase when I was a teenager and yes, even if I kept an outgoing facade, people made me cringe at times and if I didn't do what she did to them, I <i>thought</i> about it many times. Everything annoyed me, and I didn't even realize it - I was so full of shit, frankly, if I could slap my younger self I'd do it. Well, I never wanted to die, never, and some of her actions were really awful, so I'm not telling that I can understand all of Parker's decisions but anyway, <i>I get her</i>. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I still remember being hurt when the teacher made as big a fuss over my classmates' lesser efforts as she did over mine, which was perfect. Or maybe not as perfect as I thought."</b>
</blockquote><br><i>Can you understand what she's feeling?</i> Because I can. No matter how ugly it sounds, oh, man, how I get this feeling. I used to, anyway. Trying to explain why I need everything to be <i>perfect</i>, being mad when people don't get it? Oh, yes, Parker's struggles hit a nerve with me.<br><br><b>But let's go some years ago</b>. I always was this weird kid who gets straight -As and reads a lot, who never breaks the rules because never sees the point in it, whose success is <i>expected</i>, no matter what happens. Don't get fooled, I wasn't lonely, as I always could count on a solid group of friends, but I was super serious until senior year. My parents weren't really strict because 1)they trusted me and they were right to do so and 2)it was just not their way of raising us. But on my senior year, I lost it. I started to ditch school so often that school rang my parents twice a week and I developed a hell lot of tips to sneak out school without being caught. Yet my rates didn't suffer too much, because I showed up for the tests and I spent my free time reading (in France we can specialize in Junior and Senior years, and I was in Literature-Philosophy-Languages). <br><br>Why did I change all of a sudden? <br><br>The only thing I can say it's that <b>I didn't want to be <i>me</i> anymore</b>. To be frank, I wasn't full of self-loathing at all, in fact I think it was quite the opposite. Or isn't it the same thing, after all? I don't know anymore. God, I was so conceited, as it seems that only teenagers can be - I thought I got it all, and I couldn't have been more wrong, but the expectations I felt on my shoulders were suddenly too hard to stand - I'm not saying I was right, that's only what it was. <br><br><b>Why am I telling you that?</b> Because I think that's why I can relate to Parker - I can understand why she's acting out of character, or more accurately, out of what <i>others</i> assume to be her personality. Because sometimes, <b>we need to destroy a part of ourselves to evolve, because the way we are seen is suffocating us</b>. And yes, we are hurting people who love us when we are acting that way, because we disturb the way they see us and what's more unsettling than seeing our best friend, our girlfriend, our daughter suddenly changing? Although I truly think that we mustn't lie to ourselves and never deny who we are, I can't deny that it's fucking difficult to deal with these changes when we are the people who are around. Anyway, it took me <i>years</i> to learn to be less perfectionist, in my studies, in my work, in my life (I never was like Parker about my appearance, though). Because in the end, we realize that in addition to make our lives an hell, we make other lives an hell, and by others I mean people we care about. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"No one will notice how wrong you are if everything you do ends up right."</b>
</blockquote><br>Perhaps you think that it's not a review. Let me disagree : <b>if I can relate on such a strong level, that's only because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a>'s characters are so fleshed-out I feel I can grab them and see a part of myself in them</b>. Parker sure doesn't make it easy to love her, she is unapologetic, smart-ass, and straight-on bitchy at some point. But I I cared about her, deeply, as I did about Jack, Chris, and even Becky. They feel so real to me that I can't help. As usual, her <b>writing is raw, beautiful and compelling</b>, and I was hooked from the beginning. Indeed her books are such page-turners that I always know that I'll end reading them in a sitting. Not to mention that we can't help but wait to know what happened to Parker to explain why she lost it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and yes it's awful, and difficult to not hate her for this, but to me that's not the point here <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Congrats, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a>. Once again, you got me.</b> <br><br><b>Thanks so much to my incredible friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please" rel="nofollow noopener">Chelsea</a> for this birthday gift ♥<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote><a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></blockquote></b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16026982712082153904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170486094" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170486094?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170486094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10904308703338033811"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Based on what I've read so far, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers' title='Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Courtney Summers</a> is easily one of my favourite young adult authors. Her books are incredibly raw and emotional and her talent for getting inside the mind of troubled teens isn't very common in young adult literature.<br/><br/>I admit that I didn't like this book quite as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are' title='Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Some Girls Are</a> but that isn't saying a lot, it was still powerful and moving. I expected to not like this novel as much because of the lower average rating than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are' title='Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Some Girls Are</a>, but I think the m</span>
  <span id="freeText10904308703338033811" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Based on what I've read so far, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> is easily one of my favourite young adult authors. Her books are incredibly raw and emotional and her talent for getting inside the mind of troubled teens isn't very common in young adult literature.<br><br>I admit that I didn't like this book quite as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> but that isn't saying a lot, it was still powerful and moving. I expected to not like this novel as much because of the lower average rating than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a>, but I think the main reason for that is due to Parker Fadley being more difficult to relate to if you're a teenage girl reading this.<br><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> we understand the protagonist, we feel her pain when she is ostracised by people she once called best friends, and we also understand what she must be feeling to have no friends anymore and to want to be part of a 'crowd' in high school. Parker, on the other hand, wants none of this. She is moody, sarcastic, she is that character in many young adult books that is put there for you to hate, seemingly nasty for no reason.<br><br>But what if that girl who puts people down as soon as she meets them wasn't just a throwaway character meant to incite hatred? What if she was a person with thoughts and feelings and <i>reasons</i>.<br><br>This is what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> does best. She takes the cliche, the stereotypical high school bitch, and she gets inside her mind. And it's a sad, lonely and eye-opening place to be. There has never been a 'bitch', high school or otherwise, that came out of her mother's womb that way.<br><br>I truly love reading these books and I can't wait to read more by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a>. If you're just getting started with her novels, I recommend reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> first, mainly because I think that one speaks to a wider audience than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3521484.Cracked_Up_to_Be" title="Cracked Up to Be by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Cracked Up to Be</a>, which will suit some and not others.<br><br>But whatever you do, do not make the mistake that these are typical high school novels with cute boys and mean girls, the covers can be misleading that way.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10904308703338033811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1239998620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1239998620" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1239998620?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=reality-bites">reality-bites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=emotionally-intense">emotionally-intense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1239998620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15851290917908193433"><b> <i> "The sooner you make a mistake and learn to live with it, the better. You're not responsible for everything. You can't control the way things end up." </i></b> <br/><br/>Behind the sarcasm, teenage angst, and melodrama is this very powerful story and intense read that will ultimately give a very important message especially to many of our young people today obsessed with the idea of popularity and perfection.<br/><br/>Parker, an eighteen year old teenager, suddenly decides that she doesn’t want to be popular anymore and </span>
  <span id="freeText15851290917908193433" style="display:none"><b> <i> "The sooner you make a mistake and learn to live with it, the better. You're not responsible for everything. You can't control the way things end up." </i></b> <br><br>Behind the sarcasm, teenage angst, and melodrama is this very powerful story and intense read that will ultimately give a very important message especially to many of our young people today obsessed with the idea of popularity and perfection.<br><br>Parker, an eighteen year old teenager, suddenly decides that she doesn’t want to be popular anymore and so she does the complete opposites of what she used to do as the most popular girl in school. The reason behind this bravado or is it just bravado? Well, read the book to find out.^^<br><br>I honestly admire <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> for her boldness and somewhat carelessness in her writing. For instance, the use of abrupt transitions made the story even more gripping and intense. The way she managed to pique my curiosity from beginning until the very last page is fascinating.<br><br>It’s also a very rare talent to be able to portray an angsty, sarcastic, and bitchy teenage girl in a totally non-annoying way and the author did exactly that while also managing to make the character sarcastically humorous that it was never a bore reading this.<br><br> The tone is actually a perfect combination of humor and grimness contributing to the originality of the entire story.<br><br><i> <b> “I don’t see the point of being a guidance counselor in high school if you can’t have a gun.” </b></i> <br><br>The characters (although stereotyped) are very effectively portrayed and you can’t help but relate with them. There’s also one character by the name of Jake that I completely adore. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I love his persistence, humor and his weirdness over women’s monthly period. Lol.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>I just have one apprehension though. Reading this and several other YA contemporaries’ horrific portrayal of high school and the people in it makes me really fear for my future children. *Teeth chatter* <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415065321ra/11721124.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15851290917908193433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3271526441" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3271526441" />
    <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks"><img alt="BernLuvsBooks " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585010050p2/3087404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3271526441?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3271526441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3764483735793622700">Parker Fadley is perfect. She has perfect grades, she's captain of the cheerleading squad, dating the most popular boy school and has a bright future ahead of her. Until it all goes wrong and Parker finds herself starring in a new role - <i>that of the perfect mess</i>. <br/><br/>I read this book in 1 sitting. It wasn't as compelling a read for me as Sadie but I was hooked and emotionally invested in finding out what had led to Parker's unraveling. I really enjoyed the way Courtney Summers wove in the back story</span>
  <span id="freeText3764483735793622700" style="display:none">Parker Fadley is perfect. She has perfect grades, she's captain of the cheerleading squad, dating the most popular boy school and has a bright future ahead of her. Until it all goes wrong and Parker finds herself starring in a new role - <i>that of the perfect mess</i>. <br /><br />I read this book in 1 sitting. It wasn't as compelling a read for me as Sadie but I was hooked and emotionally invested in finding out what had led to Parker's unraveling. I really enjoyed the way Courtney Summers wove in the back story, revealing a small bit at a time. Many might find Parker unlikable but I saw a girl trying desperately to push others away in an attempt to deal with something that was obviously traumatic and overwhelming. I felt bad for her and loved how Jake saw through the armor and caught glimpses of the girl underneath it all. <br /><br />This one has strong themes - <i>suicide, rape, underage drinking, depression, anxiety and panic attacks</i>. I thought it was emotional and dark but the ending left me filled with hope. This was a strong debut and I'm glad it was rereleased. <b>Courtney Summers is a must read author!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3764483735793622700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36659049" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36659049?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=signed-books">signed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36659049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12809280891143644446">This book was everything that I hoped it was going to be and then some. And I wish that I was a good writer so that I could write a review worthy of this book. Why can’t I just say that I loved it and that it was one of the most compelling books I’ve ever read and that just be enough? Because really I don’t know why I like any book, I just do. But if I must, I guess I will. <br/><br/>The writing. If I hadn’t known that this was Summers’ debut novel, I wouldn’t have believed it. One of my most favorite boo</span>
  <span id="freeText12809280891143644446" style="display:none">This book was everything that I hoped it was going to be and then some. And I wish that I was a good writer so that I could write a review worthy of this book. Why can’t I just say that I loved it and that it was one of the most compelling books I’ve ever read and that just be enough? Because really I don’t know why I like any book, I just do. But if I must, I guess I will. <br /><br />The writing. If I hadn’t known that this was Summers’ debut novel, I wouldn’t have believed it. One of my most favorite books of all time is Speak by Laurie Halse Anderson, and this book parallels it’s greatness, it may even surpass it. Yeah it’s that good. I hope to be reading Summers in the future, she is an author to watch. <br /><br />I don’t want to get into the plot so much, because I want everyone to go in without any predispositions, well at least I don’t personally want to give anything away, I’m sure if you do some digging you can find some things out, but believe me, you don’t want to. I will say this much, I thought I had it figured out and I was wrong wrong wrong, and that is usually not the case. I found this somewhere and I don’t remember where, but it totally sums this book up: “A frightening and sobering look at the cruelty and viciousness that pervade much of contemporary high school life, as real as today's headlines.” Yeah I really wish I had written that myself. This book does not have a sugary coating. Which only makes me like it even more. <br /><br />And the characters, particularly perfect Parker Fadley, make this book an UNFORGETTABLE read. <br /><br />Would I recommend it, absolutely. Have I already been recommending it, you better believe it. <br /><br />Who knew it was so hard to be perfect. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12809280891143644446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_230568619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230568619" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/230568619?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230568619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11004907513788882250">So, I guess I just read these in opposite order…3…2…1. It’s hard to pick a favorite but this one definitely hits the closest to home. I don’t know why, but I had it in my head that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3521484.Cracked_Up_to_Be' title='Cracked Up to Be by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cracked Up to Be</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are' title='Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Some Girls Are</a> were going to be similar novels – like twin manifestos on the psychology of mean girls. Parker and Regina may both sort into the mean girl category, but they are <i>completely</i> different, as are these two novels. I think that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are' title='Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Some Girls Are</a> is a book about moving forward and away, but t</span>
  <span id="freeText11004907513788882250" style="display:none">So, I guess I just read these in opposite order…3…2…1. It’s hard to pick a favorite but this one definitely hits the closest to home. I don’t know why, but I had it in my head that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3521484.Cracked_Up_to_Be" title="Cracked Up to Be by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Cracked Up to Be</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> were going to be similar novels – like twin manifestos on the psychology of mean girls. Parker and Regina may both sort into the mean girl category, but they are <i>completely</i> different, as are these two novels. I think that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> is a book about moving forward and away, but this book is about moving inward; it’s about going back to where you lost control.<br /><br />Parker was popular, captain of the cheerleading squad, at the top of her class, and in a long term relationship with Chris, her male counterpart. Now she’s failing, drinking in school, and sabotaging her friendships. She may not even graduate. It all seems to relate back to a party last spring, but what really happened? <br /><br />I may not have loved every character in this book, but I felt like I knew them all. Parker will probably be hard to sympathize with, but she’s nauseatingly familiar to me. I think that a large part of my teenage self <i>was</i> Parker Fadley. Parker may be a gorgeous, former queen bee/cheerleading captain, while I…uh…wasn’t, but that really doesn’t matter. Courtney Summers has portrayed Parker’s inner self: her anxiety, her guilt, and her self-imposed exile with such complete definition that it doesn’t matter what her outer circumstances are. For me, it’s impossible not to relate to Parker. <br /><br />The supporting cast is also completely well-defined. There are two boys in the picture, but I would never call this a love triangle. Both characters have moments of mature sensitivity and kindness, but Courtney Summers never shies away from letting them be realistic teenage boys – sex-obsessed idiocy and all. The insecure and bitter rival Becky still managed to tug at my sympathy.<br /><br />If you love uncompromising reality in your contemporary YA’s, then you definitely need to check out Courtney Summers. Toward the end I had a few worried moments, when I feared that Parker would become a soft, repentant, <i>healed</i> person, or that everything would get wrapped up with a big happily ever after for Parker’s new relationship. But I really should have known better. Summers stays true to Parker’s bitchy, insulting, defensive voice. The relationship isn’t a magic balm that’s going to heal all of her issues; only she can do that. And it’s going to take a lot of work. The ending is hopeful, but still stays true to reality. <br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Fiona Apple – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=u_z58EZdsHE" rel="nofollow noopener">Fast As You Can</a><br /><br />Fiona Apple: creating anthems for angry bitches since 1996. <br /><br />Parker brings me so uncomfortably close to my former self that I had to choose something that I listened to as a 16 year old (probably while shut up in my room, hating myself and brooding). This song is a warning - get away from me before I screw you over. <br /><br />Also seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/04/ya-review-cracked-up-to-be-by-courtney-summers.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11004907513788882250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14859793521406700702">3.5 stars<br/> Originally published in 2008, the publisher decided to re-release the book after the recent popularity of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34810320.Sadie' title='Sadie by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'> Sadie</a>. A book that I had crowned my favorite read of 2018! In <i> Cracked Up to Be</i>, we meet the unforgettable and very unlikeable Parker Fadley.   <span id="freeText14859793521406700702" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /> Originally published in 2008, the publisher decided to re-release the book after the recent popularity of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34810320.Sadie" title="Sadie by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener"> Sadie</a>. A book that I had crowned my favorite read of 2018! In <i> Cracked Up to Be</i>, we meet the unforgettable and very unlikeable Parker Fadley. Parker is a cheerleader that doesn't cheer so much anymore and in fact, speaks biting words to all around her. Her parents appear to tiptoe around her and there are many illusions made in the story that Parker's behavior is linked to her best friend's disappearance. To say that Parker is damaged, would be an understatement, as she has to report to mandatory meetings with a counselor, is failing school and often shows up at school drunk. None of her former cheer mates or her ex-boyfriend seems to be able to get through to her, but new student Jake might finally be able to break Parker's steel fortress.<br /><br /> The mysterious circumstances that lead to Parker's downfall and her crusty exterior kept me reading. Parker was a good girl gone bad and I just needed to get to the bottom of it. Of course, the ending is left to the reader's interpretation, but I closed my book hoping that for Parker, there is health and happiness at the end of the tunnel. <br /><br /><i> Thanks to St. Martin's Press and NetGalley for an egalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br /> Publication Date 04/02/20<br /> Goodreads review 15/02/20</span>

<div id="review_230587096" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230587096" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/230587096?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781455823413" href="/book/show/10874548-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those readers who do not require their characters to be likable</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Emily May, Catie
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230587096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer998597684568069823">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/cracked-up-to-be-by-courtney-summers1.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/><br/>3.5 stars<br/><br/>The more of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers' title='Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Courtney Summers</a> I read, the more her work reminds me of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19093.Sara_Zarr' title='Sara Zarr' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sara Zarr</a>'s. They write vastly different characters - Zarr's are more subdued, quiet; Summers' are often in-your-face obnoxious and loud. But what is similar about these two authors is how well-realized their narrators' voices are. Zarr's and Summers' characters are unique and real, often unlikable, but always unforgettable.<br/><br/>The protagonist of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3521484.Cracked_Up_to_Be' title='Cracked Up to Be by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cracked Up to Be</a>, Parker, is hard to like. She is </span>
  <span id="freeText998597684568069823" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/cracked-up-to-be-by-courtney-summers1.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br /><br />3.5 stars<br /><br />The more of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> I read, the more her work reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19093.Sara_Zarr" title="Sara Zarr" rel="nofollow noopener">Sara Zarr</a>'s. They write vastly different characters - Zarr's are more subdued, quiet; Summers' are often in-your-face obnoxious and loud. But what is similar about these two authors is how well-realized their narrators' voices are. Zarr's and Summers' characters are unique and real, often unlikable, but always unforgettable.<br /><br />The protagonist of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3521484.Cracked_Up_to_Be" title="Cracked Up to Be by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Cracked Up to Be</a>, Parker, is hard to like. She is brash and sarcastic, offends and lashes out at everyone who cares about her - parents, friends, teachers. There is a reason behind her self-destructive, self-punishing and antagonistic behavior, and it's a big one. You won't like Parker even when you find out her secret, you might even hate her then. But, with all that, she is still a human being worthy of understanding and maybe empathy or, possibly, forgiveness. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3521484.Cracked_Up_to_Be" title="Cracked Up to Be by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Cracked Up to Be</a> is a strong debut. I don't think the climax of the story was constructed the best way it could have been. The last few chapters are a little messy. But I do like how the novel ended. There are consequences to Parker's sins, but there is a hope for her break from the abyss of self-hate too. There are mistakes in our lives that we need to forgive ourselves for, just to survive. Even if they are as heavy as Parker's.</span>
  <a data-text-id="998597684568069823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1001648211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1001648211" />
    <a title="Hillary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18999155-hillary"><img alt="Hillary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601752862p2/18999155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1001648211?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hillary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hillary" href="/user/show/18999155-hillary">Hillary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18999155-hillary?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1001648211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9309064361812329385">I will try to write something that makes sense about this book, unlike what my old self wrote years ago *cries in cringe*<br/><br/>This book was my least favorite Courtney Summers even when I first read it, but at the time I had just started reading and reviewing books on here. Which means I didn't really know how to explain why I liked or I didn't like a book, and my reviews where biased... ha ha, fun times. I'm glad to see I was still able to notice if a book was well written or not, though.<br/><br/>I didn't rem</span>
  <span id="freeText9309064361812329385" style="display:none">I will try to write something that makes sense about this book, unlike what my old self wrote years ago *cries in cringe*<br /><br />This book was my least favorite Courtney Summers even when I first read it, but at the time I had just started reading and reviewing books on here. Which means I didn't really know how to explain why I liked or I didn't like a book, and my reviews where biased... ha ha, fun times. I'm glad to see I was still able to notice if a book was well written or not, though.<br /><br />I didn't remember a lot about this book (and definitely NOTHING about an animal death, I'm shook), only the twist. The book is enjoyable and very raw and gritty, typical Courtney Summers, and it stays with you for a while after you finish it, but at the same time it's forgettable, thing that comes from the plot having little to no structure. In comparison to this author's next books, this one goes out in circles and doesn't give the reader enough evidence to figure out the main character. The actual reveal is twenty pages from the end and it's too late.<br /><br />What saves this book is the characters and mental illness representation. <br /><br />All characters are very well-rounded, their motivations stand out and make them feel real. Each one of them has a part in the book, it's not just about Parker, so you unwillingly end up understanding each and everyone of them (even Becky). I especially love how Chris and Jake were written, they don't fall into stereotypes and make a blend of very mature and immature decisions that I find super appropriate for their age. They are responsible guys and I wish I had the opportunity to have boy friends like them when I was 18. Jake is straight-up ADORABLE, I want to pinch his cheeks so bad 😳<br /><br />I know it's supposed to happen, but I'm always surprised when I reread a book years after I read it for the first time in my teen years and I find out I have different feelings about it. In this case, I relate to this book much more than before, because Parker has PTSD and panic attacks, and while I don't have PTSD (thank god), I've had my fair share of panic attacks in the last years. Parker made me feel seen and represented, and I literally have no idea if this is a bad or good thing for me. Nonetheless, this means the book has stellar representation for this kind of mental illness. It's good the book ends how it ends because it teaches that therapy is a friend, not an enemy. I'd love to see this book on a school reading list against the stigmatization of mental support.<br /><br />This book has aged well in the last ten years and I would still recommend it, but it needs to be said that the main character inappropriately makes use of the term "anorexic" to describe another character. While this character has his own mental illness and eating disorder, I felt uncomfortable seeing that adjective used to refer to a very thin person as if it were interchangeable.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>I get caught up in outcomes. I convince myself they're truths. No one will notice how wrong you are if everything you do ends up right.The rest becomes incidental. So incidental that, after a while, you forget. Maybe you are perfect. Good. It must be true. Who can argue with results? You're not so wrong after all. So you buy into it and you go crazy maintaining it. Except it creeps up on you sometimes, that you're not right. Imperfect. Bad.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />******<br /><br />December 2014, first read review<br /><br />I can see how the author’s style has evolved through the years. This book is her debut, and I found it wonderful, but not like her two successive books I’ve read before this one.<br />The difference is minimal, though. Maybe I liked Eddie and Sloane a little more than Parker.<br />Sometimes I wanted to shake Parker so hard, and then other times I was like "yeah, that's how my head works!" I'm allergic to people, you know. Just like Parker.<br />I really loved both Chris and Jake.<br />The author has talent in creating open endings that suit perfectly the entire narrative.<br />Every time I read a book of hers I’m reminded again of why she’s my favorite author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9309064361812329385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_150858576" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150858576" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150858576?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=kcls">kcls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=wishlist-for-dtbs-to-keep">wishlist-for-dtbs-to-keep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150858576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11847513101380209106">Parker Fadley used to be head cheerleader. She had perfect grades and a perfect boyfriend. Fast forward a few months and she is drinking heavily, treating everybody like crap (though this hasn’t changed much), broken up with her boyfriend, and missing every single homework deadline. What happened to cause her decline? <br/><br/>When I was in high school, I had to wear a uniform. Since it was an all-girls Catholic school, my morning went something like this:<br/>6:00—alarm goes off. Snooze.<br/>6:15—alarm goes off. </span>
  <span id="freeText11847513101380209106" style="display:none">Parker Fadley used to be head cheerleader. She had perfect grades and a perfect boyfriend. Fast forward a few months and she is drinking heavily, treating everybody like crap (though this hasn’t changed much), broken up with her boyfriend, and missing every single homework deadline. What happened to cause her decline? <br /><br />When I was in high school, I had to wear a uniform. Since it was an all-girls Catholic school, my morning went something like this:<br />6:00—alarm goes off. Snooze.<br />6:15—alarm goes off. Snooze.<br />6:30—alarm goes off. Snooze<br />6:45—roll out of bed wearing t-shirt and boxers. Put on socks. Pick up polo shirt, kilt, and clogs from floor. Brush teeth.<br />7:00-7:30—drive to school. Eat granola bar. In school parking lot, put polo and kilt on over pajamas. <br />Proceed with day.<br /><br />This is funny to me because Parker’s hungover/total mess description basically aligns with my every day of high school look. I don’t remember brushing my hair for four years. But, thankfully, I wasn’t such a psychological mess. The narrative in this book basically follows Parker in the present day but snippets of the night “it” happened are interspersed in the text until it all unravels. I found this both intriguing and annoying; the latter because the night kept building up little by little but what we already knew was repeated. (x, then x and y, then x and y and z) By the end, I was practically shouting at the book, “I GET IT! I KNOW XYZABCDEFGHI happened. Just frakking tell me already!” (though I already had it figured out)<br /><br />But you’ll notice that I gave this one four stars. I love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a>’ writing style. She writes the horrifically mean girl like no one else. (more prominently in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a>) Her characters are realistically flawed and you can almost smell the desperation that drips off of nearly every one of them, whether they are desperate for friendship, love, or forgiveness for missteps. This book isn’t for everyone for that reason—it is a frustrating read because you see all of these characters trying to help Parker find what she is looking for and she walks all over them and manipulates their feelings. I don’t know if I could have the patience for her that several of her peers did, especially considering I didn’t have much patience for her as a reader. <br /><br />The “love triangle” (if you can call it that) in this book was a little bizarre. Parker’s ex-boyfriend Chris is still in love with her and will basically do anything for her. The more-like-a-love-square is filled out with Parker, Chris’s new girlfriend who is Parker’s frenemy, and new guy Jake, who is attempting to get Parker to open up about what happened. Flash! Bang! Drama! Anyway, Courtney Summers lovers will find the same old awesome in this one: gritty topic, beautiful writing, a bitchity main girl, and a lightning fast read.<br /><br />Shoutout to Cory, who interviewed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> last week at <a>The Book Lantern</a>.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11847513101380209106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
