<div id="review_1253093535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1253093535" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7463065-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420145167p2/7463065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1253093535?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/7463065-penny">Penny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781455823413" href="/book/show/10874548-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7463065-penny?shelf=y-read-young-adults">y-read-young-adults</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7463065-penny?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7463065-penny?shelf=likereviews">likereviews</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1253093535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9128837716814686102">This is one of those times when I seem to have read a completely different book from everyone else.<br/><br/><b>It was uninteresting and pointless. It sure wasn't moving or emotional to me.</b><br/><br/>We get into the mind of the bich/ex-"perfect" girl at school. I had the feeling that I was supposed to be sorry for her once we knew what her thoughts were, but that didn't happen for me. So what? It's not as if we don't know everyone has feelings no matter how good or bad they are. What she was thinking and feeling toward</span>
  <span id="freeText9128837716814686102" style="display:none">This is one of those times when I seem to have read a completely different book from everyone else.<br /><br /><b>It was uninteresting and pointless. It sure wasn't moving or emotional to me.</b><br /><br />We get into the mind of the bich/ex-"perfect" girl at school. I had the feeling that I was supposed to be sorry for her once we knew what her thoughts were, but that didn't happen for me. So what? It's not as if we don't know everyone has feelings no matter how good or bad they are. What she was thinking and feeling towards herself was completely deserved, for the rest part she was a bit heartless. So I don't see the point in this book. <br /><br />Parker changes after some kind of trauma she experienced. Her family, friends and teachers are trying to cope with this change while being lenient with her and trying to help her over and over again. I can't believe how all the people around her are such pushovers and masochistic. I don't understand where all their care is coming from. <br /><br />Parker is a bich, unbelievably selfish and a horrible person. I don't care that she has issues, everyone has them. That doesn't explain or excuse anything about her. I might understand where she is coming from but that does not excuses or forgives her. Everything is on her and I can't pity her or sympathize with her seeing as she has so many people that care about her when she doesn't even deserve them. Her problems were caused by her own choices, and beside the fact of her felling rightly guilty about what she did, or better yet, about <b>what she didn't do and should undoubtedly have done</b>, I didn't see her trying to rectify anything. <br /><br /><b>I am confused as to what this book is trying to say, or if it is trying to say something at all, because I sure don't see it, it's completely pointless. </b> However, it does make me mad to have wasted my time with this ugly story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9128837716814686102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I DONT WANT THIS KIND OF PAIN<br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br />#4 and last book with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26402455" rel="nofollow noopener">saunta</a> in our <i>

    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257754620?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257754620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9173440251389228875">4.5 stars.<br/><br/><i>Slight spoilers follow…</i><br/><br/><br/><i>
  <b>“I’d rather be certifiable than perpetually boring.”</b>
</i><br/><br/><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br/>ME TOO!<br/><br/><b>High Points.</b><br/>I loved everything: the writing, the characters, the emotions, the subject. <br/>Done.<br/>*bats off hands*<br/><br/><b>Low Points.</b><br/>This book was so small it could get lost in my back teeth.<br/>I’m just being selfish because I wanted to spend more time with this book but <i>hey</i>, if book reviewers can’t be selfish then who can?<br/>That is the<i> real</i> question, I think. <br/><br/><b>Heroine.</b><br/>You know how I really l</span>
  <span id="freeText9173440251389228875" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br /><i>Slight spoilers follow…</i><br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>“I’d rather be certifiable than perpetually boring.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br />ME TOO!<br /><br /><b>High Points.</b><br />I loved everything: the writing, the characters, the emotions, the subject. <br />Done.<br />*bats off hands*<br /><br /><b>Low Points.</b><br />This book was so small it could get lost in my back teeth.<br />I’m just being selfish because I wanted to spend more time with this book but <i>hey</i>, if book reviewers can’t be selfish then who can?<br />That is the<i> real</i> question, I think. <br /><br /><b>Heroine.</b><br />You know how I really like my heroines to be decent human beings?<br />Well, I really <i>really</i> like my heroines to be bitches. <br />And I don’t mean the uh-oh-she-has-blonde-hair-and-she’s-a-cheerleader (or the British equivalent which is… um, something)-and-her-boyfriend-is-smokin’-and-has-hidden-depths-and-probably-will-end-up-with-the-heroine kinda bitch. <br />I mean, like, real bitches.<br />Parker is no cookie cutter bitch.<br />She is brilliant and I’m saying no more because I don’t want to spoil things.<br /><br />Except that I have a total girlcrush on her and I have a feeling it’s all going to end in tears. <br /><br /><b>Love Interest(s).</b><br />Eh, who am I kidding?<br />This is Parker’s story… these boys didn’t even had a look in. <br /><br /><b>Theme Tune.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VHC8vuBU9rg" rel="nofollow noopener">Girls Like You by The Naked and Famous. </a><br /><br /><br /><b>Sadness Scale </b><br />7/10.<br />I’ve never understood the belief that a book can only be classed as having a happy ending if the MC gets with the boy/girl.<br />Surely the reader, if they really connected with a character, would want to see them battle fearlessly against what is plaguing them and destroying them from the inside?<br />With that in mind,and only a <i>slight</i> implied spoiler, this is one of the happiest and hopeful endings I’ve read in a long time. <br /><br />The subject matter of Cracked Up to Be (secrets) has been done before; but never quite like this. <br />It’s remarkable that a book of only 200 pages can be so rich and dense with realistic emotions. <br />So, bravo Ms Summers. Bravo. <br />Oh and also, it took me about three hours to read this book.<br />Coincidentally that was half the amount of time it took me to get over one scene, towards the end. Jeez louise. Was that necessary?! WAS IT?!<br /><br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />People who don’t believe that the purpose of boys in literature is to solve every problem that faces the heroine. People who like their heroines with a bit of spark…and sadistic, manipulative and incredibly clever. People who get frustrated when authors can’t handle a flashback (MS Summers can, by the by). People who look for deeper-meanings in art projects. People whose idea of “romantic” is no underwear. People who don’t get overly attached to fictional critters.<br /><br />You can read this review and lots of other exciting things on my blog <a href="http://weartheoldcoat.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>

  <i>This could have been easily a 4 star read for me apart from the ending.</i>

  <span id="freeText8346039170036890046" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>This could have been easily a 4 star read for me apart from the ending.</i>
</b><br><br>I did not know what to expect when I started with this, the cover makes it feel like a light YA read, the blurb makes it sound more serious.<br><br>The sum it up, this is about Parker and the changes that have come in her life because of something that has happened to her.... This was the suspense bit, which is revealed at the end and did not somehow add up with the overall story for me..<br><br>Parker is beautiful, top of her class, going out with the most popular guy and at the top of the pecking order in her high school. <br><br><b>
  <i>I didn't want to be popular because it was easier; I wanted to be popular because in high school that's the best thing you can be: perfect. Everything else is shit.</i>
</b><br><br>But something has gone wrong, she has broken up with her boyfriend, is drinking and no more interested in studies, it feels more like Parker is not interested in life anymore...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470363711i/19919465.jpg" height="" width="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Somehow I expected Parker's ex-boyfriend to be a douche bag but he is actually really sweet. Jake Gardner and Parker's relation is really interesting. The author has dived into the the typical high-school cliche and come-up with more vulnerable aspects of each and every typical high-school character.<br><br>The story even though focused on a a destructive character still has humor and Parker even though depressed is very spunky.<br><br><b>The ending was a bit out of sync and a bit of a let down</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She gets drunk 1 night, sees her friend getting raped, does not do anything and the next morning also does not say anything. What the hell!! And this thought is destroying her. She loves her friend but just let's her friends disappearance go without taking any action. Throughout the story she is depressed and we know maybe she has done something wrong, but this just does not make sense... Maybe it's about how she is not perfect anymore but it did not go down with me <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I felt the ending somehow could have been different and better....<br><br><b>
  <i>This is a first read by this author for me and I really liked how the story flows. I will definitely be checking out more books by her.</i>

<div id="review_3163517785" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3163517785" />
    <a title="Cortney LaScola - The Bookworm Myrtle Beach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6320671-cortney-lascola---the-bookworm-myrtle-beach"><img alt="Cortney LaScola - The Bookworm Myrtle Beach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581434254p2/6320671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3163517785?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cortney LaScola - The Bookworm Myrtle Beach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cortney LaScola - The Bookworm Myrtle Beach" href="/user/show/6320671-cortney-lascola---the-bookworm-myrtle-beach">Cortney LaScola - The Bookworm Myrtle Beach</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7083994445547577006">This wasn't an easy book to read... it was sad and upsetting, but I'm really glad I did. There is something about Courtney Summers' writing that is just so real. Even with how self-destructive Parker was, you couldn't help rooting for her. </span>

<div id="review_95530367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95530367" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95530367?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95530367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3602862060792549444">Cracked up to Be by Courtney Summers is probably one of the more difficult reads I’ve encountered in the YA genre. The protagonist, Parker Fadley, was flawed, damaged and on a downward spiral. In most cases, that’s enough cause to have me sympathize for a main character, but the way the story developed, she never really pulled at my heartstrings. I carried more angst for her ex-boyfriend Chris, and the new guy Jake that was dumb enough to fall for her. She really put everyone in her life through</span>
  <span id="freeText3602862060792549444" style="display:none">Cracked up to Be by Courtney Summers is probably one of the more difficult reads I’ve encountered in the YA genre. The protagonist, Parker Fadley, was flawed, damaged and on a downward spiral. In most cases, that’s enough cause to have me sympathize for a main character, but the way the story developed, she never really pulled at my heartstrings. I carried more angst for her ex-boyfriend Chris, and the new guy Jake that was dumb enough to fall for her. She really put everyone in her life through the ringer, and I know I should be compelled to give her some slack because of what she faced, but nope, I really couldn’t. Her heartlessness must have rubbed off on me.<br /><br />About the story... Parker Fadley is every parent’s dream child. She is an honors student with distinction, meaning she has a perfect 4.0, she’s head cheerleader, her boyfriend is one of the most popular boys in their school, they are running champions of the winter formal king and queen, and just about everything Parker attempts, she does it with perfection. Unfortunately, all that changes one fateful night at a party Chris hosts and from that day forward, Parker is put on suicide watch, her grades fall to the point where she might not graduate, and she quits the cheer team. That’s not all that changes, she begins to push people away in a destructive manner, and it’s considered a good day if she shows up to school sober.<br /><br />This story was interesting to the point that I wanted to find out what really happened that night that destroyed Parker. I was reading to hopefully come across a full conflict reveal and eventual resolution. Well, neither of that happens.<br /><br />I’m removing two stars for a few reasons. One, I had a difficult time with how the back-story to Parker’s destruction was revealed. As the story progressed, a part of that fateful night was uncovered one piece at a time. But each time additional back-story was presented, the complete night was repeated. It came to be annoying after the fourth time. Another issue I had with the book had to do with Jake and Chris. They were extremely likeable characters in the book, and the ending for them was unfulfilling by more than a mile IMO. WT?? Is that all they get after everything Parker put them through? I was a little irritated to say the least. In addition, there was a major event that occurred the night Parker’s life turned upside down and when it was finally revealed the details were fuzzy and unclear. After hearing the story repeat itself over half a dozen times, you’d think the author would get the ending spot on… she really didn’t.<br /><br />Overall, it’s an okay read, but I didn’t really pull any life lessons nor did I experience any significant emotional journey. Not a waste of time, just nothing to brag about.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3602862060792549444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_202613649" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202613649" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/202613649?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202613649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3994320857384845827">Already being a big fan of Courtney Summers since I read This Is Not a Test, I knew before going into this that it was going to be a ride with a lot of feels! So much feels!<br/><br/>Parker is the definition of a snarky bitch. She has an attitude you want to slap her for, but as a protagonist she's especially amusing and definitely entertaining. The used-to-be cheerleading captain turned angry emo tells us that something has happened to this girl to change her so drastically. This "something" is told to u</span>
  <span id="freeText3994320857384845827" style="display:none">Already being a big fan of Courtney Summers since I read This Is Not a Test, I knew before going into this that it was going to be a ride with a lot of feels! So much feels!<br><br>Parker is the definition of a snarky bitch. She has an attitude you want to slap her for, but as a protagonist she's especially amusing and definitely entertaining. The used-to-be cheerleading captain turned angry emo tells us that something has happened to this girl to change her so drastically. This "something" is told to us via strange behavior from Parker which seem insignificant at first, but as the book progresses the feeling gets more urgent, and is mixed with flashbacks that leaves us wondering what the heck exactly happened here. These flashbacks gets longer at each telling; every time she remembers, she gets thrown a little deeper into this blocked memory that, in the end, weaves itself together into an emotionally distressing story. We don't get to fully understand the reason behind her intense attitude until the very end. Still, you know something happened; you know she did not choose to be this way, something broke her, made her bitter. For this reason I found it easy to look past her bitchiness and feel bad for whatever it is that she is going through. It also helps that Courtney has a way of creating genuine characters. Characters that are easy to sympathize with no matter their outward personality, because it's clear this crappy attitude is only a front, something Parker is hiding behind.<br><br>I already feel like I summed up this whole book in that mere paragraph. It's a fairly short read and while the plot is compelling from start to finish with amazing characters, energy, and <i>the feels</i>, it's hard to get into the thick of it since it consists of layer after layer of answers that eventually come full circle for the big reveal. By far, the best part of the novel is Parker herself. Full of attitude and energy, she tells us this story in the best way she can: amidst snark and outbursts. She hardly remembers what happened herself, though she's slowly regaining her memory of this horrific event that we're in the midst of discovering alongside her. When we do finally get the whole story, I did have to go over the reveal a couple of times to get everything straight. Some of the details come out a little fuzzy at the end. This is likely due to the same memory being repeated throughout the book which ultimately connects under different circumstances than we first had imagined. We're left to mold these memories to fit a tragic event that once seemed innocent; it changes our perspective of it all. Moving on to the ending itself, I thought it was memorable, realistic, and we come to understand Parker completely. However, I did find the romantic aspect's conclusion a tad underwhelming. I expected something… different, and was more than disappointed by the unfair finality of it all. Call me a romantic at heart?<br><br>Cracked Up to Be is an emotional foray into the gritty reality that is PTSD. Parker is not here for you to like her; her arrogant personality and unabashed attitude is a way out, out of the guilt that is almost literally eating her alive. Like This Is Not a Test, this one is for the fans of sharp and unapologetic contemps! And if you love audiobooks, the narrator nailed Parker's voice!<br><br>--<br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236618i/681468.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover">don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204597852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2148161370805408386"><b>*I Don't Know How Many Stars*</b><br/><br/>Guys. I am so lost for words. This book made me feel things I just can't even...can't even. I liked it and I hated it. I loved it but wanted to punch it. I was obsessed with it and I wasn't obsessed with it. I couldn't put it down but when I did I felt a little bit lighter. I don't even know what to say, so how should I understand how to rate it?<br/><br/><b>Jake should know-well, everyone should know-there's no such thing as a decent human being. It's just an illusion.<br/>And when i</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2148161370805408386" style="display:none"><b>*I Don't Know How Many Stars*</b><br><br>Guys. I am so lost for words. This book made me feel things I just can't even...can't even. I liked it and I hated it. I loved it but wanted to punch it. I was obsessed with it and I wasn't obsessed with it. I couldn't put it down but when I did I felt a little bit lighter. I don't even know what to say, so how should I understand how to rate it?<br><br><b>Jake should know-well, everyone should know-there's no such thing as a decent human being. It's just an illusion.<br>And when it's gone, it's really gone.</b><br><br><b>I rate based on how I feel</b>....and I just don't know what I feel. I keep (in my head) going from a 4 to a 3 to a 2 to a 3.5 to a 4. Because, like with all Courtney Summers novels, I felt ALL emotions...but they were different this time. <b>I felt them more intensely.</b> And not necessarily in a good way. One minute I was happy, the next I was sad and aching for more and I just wasn't able to put a pin on what exactly worked for me. And, in the end, I wanted more for this horribly fucked up character and I don't know I don't know I don't knooooow. I just still can't express how I feel.<br><br><b>I get caught up in outcomes. I convince myself they're truths. No one will notice how wrong you are if everything you do ends up right. The rest becomes incidental. So incidental that, after a while, you forget. Maybe you are perfect. Good. It must be true. Who can argue with results? You're not so wrong after all. So you buy into it and you go crazy maintaining it. Except it creeps up on you sometimes, that you're not right. Imperfect. Bad. So you snap your fingers and it goes away.<br>Until something you can't ignore happens and you see it all over yourself.</b><br><br>I felt like I was underneath a microscope. I felt as if my brain was pried open like a gaping wound for everyone to see, because I just couldn't put a mask on my displeasure or my happiness or my crying and it was like this raw, ripping open of my soul because poor Parker. Poor, poor Parker. I couldn't stand how she treated Jake but I understood it. I hated when she pushed him away or made him think she felt less about him than she really did....because that's what she wanted. She <i>wanted</i> people to hate her, she <i>wanted</i> to fade into the background. And it just hurt me so deeply when she would push people away....because 'that's how it had to be.'<br><br><b>I lean against the door. I should be sitting so we can have our weekly session where I pick the lint off my skirt and determinedly maintain my silence while she stares at me, except today I have to break that silence. And all for a boy, too. How degrading.</b><br><br>This book was a lot like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/680842973?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Unteachable</i>
</a> for me. I gave that book a 4 even though it depressed me 90% of the time because despite all that...I couldn't put it down, ya know? What does that say? <br><br><b>The writing.</b> Wow, the writing. It always transports me to another world and I adore this author and I guess I should know a star rating but I can't put a finger on what feels right...and that's how I always choose. It just <i>feels</i> right when I think of a rating. When I click a star, I release all this built up energy because everything falls into place and fits so perfectly with my review. But when I think of clicking a star here, nothing fits. Not for this story.<br><br><b>"See you tomorrow," I call after her.<br>She stops, turns and gives me a hilariously quizzical look.<br>It could be worth it for this alone.<br>"What?"<br>"I'll see you tomorrow. For the semi-formal? You, me, Chris and Jake." I force a big smile at her. "I'm really looking forward to it."<br>I'm such a bitch, but Becky makes it so easy.</b><br><br>So...this wasn't a review. And I don't really care if anyone reads it or doesn't read it because I can't give people an honest answer. I loved a lot of parts. But I also hated a lot of parts, as well. I suppose I could break it down a little for you guys, just as an end note?<br><br><b>Loved:</b><br><br>-Jake<br>-Writing<br>-Story/plot in general<br>-The Humor<br>-Parker's snark towards everyone, it made me laugh a lot (She's such a bitch)<br><br><b>Liked:</b><br><br>-Parker <br>-How she put her walls up <br>-Her family <br>-The mystery behind why she is the way she is<br><br><b>Didn't love at all:</b><br><br>-Animal (That's all I'll say on that matter)<br>-Becky. Annoying bitch<br>-The conclusion. I really really really wanted more, but I understood it, as well<br>-How Jake was treated (It was sometimes funny, but other times it broke my heart)<br><br><br>So. You know. There you go. <br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

    <a title="Bren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61659069-bren"><img alt="Bren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590193281p2/61659069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2795816155?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bren" href="/user/show/61659069-bren">Bren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=realistic-young-adult-fiction">realistic-young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=social-issues">social-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=better-or-worse-than-expected">better-or-worse-than-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=read-and-reviewed">read-and-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=dark-and-heavy">dark-and-heavy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2795816155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer875973815114105397">“I take a deep breath. It smells suspiciously like bullshit in here.” <br/>― Courtney Summers, Cracked Up to Be<br/><br/>Review to follow.<br/><br/>I feel badly giving this book two stars. I do. It was a dark thought provoking read, fascinating in it's way. But I had some issues with it.<br/><br/>I do wish Goodreads did half stars. But they don't.<br/><br/>So I had read another book by this author, "Some girls are'. I loved it! This one took me longer to read and though I was moved, here are some of my issues.<br/><br/>First off..SPOILERS:<br/><br/>Second off</span>
  <span id="freeText875973815114105397" style="display:none">“I take a deep breath. It smells suspiciously like bullshit in here.” <br />― Courtney Summers, Cracked Up to Be<br /><br />Review to follow.<br /><br />I feel badly giving this book two stars. I do. It was a dark thought provoking read, fascinating in it's way. But I had some issues with it.<br /><br />I do wish Goodreads did half stars. But they don't.<br /><br />So I had read another book by this author, "Some girls are'. I loved it! This one took me longer to read and though I was moved, here are some of my issues.<br /><br />First off..SPOILERS:<br /><br />Second off..THE DOG!<br /><br />Anyone who knows me knows I take off a star or two for animal violence. Especially when it isn't needed and you can see it coming from a mile away.<br /><br />I don't get why authors do it. I am not the only one. I see so many people who this gimmick upsets..what is the point?<br /><br />In this book's case ..what did killing off the dog add to the story? Really? I knew it was gonna happen too. Immediately. I really found it distasteful. Maybe I am just not the right person to read this book.<br /><br />Then there is Parker. I felt for her. But..I am not clear on the ending and why she did what she did. I am not blaming but it is never told. Not Parker telling Jessie about the Evan's cheating. I am clear on that. But about witnessing the rape/kidnapping and what happened after? Why did she not scream "Jessie's being kidnapped"? I am not blaming Parker and there were moments I sure felt for her. Alot. But I did not get the MOTIVATION..what was behind it.<br /><br />Then the book ends. So after investing all that emotional energy we never do find out..anything really. So..what was the point?<br /><br />Parker was obviously experiencing PTSD and I felt for her. She wasn't a bad person. Nobody should EVER reach that point and I was originally going to give this book a 3 or 4 because the author did a good job in making me care about a character whose motivations I did not understand.<br /><br />Until the dog died. And so much time was spent on that.<br /><br />And the book finally just..ends..and we the reader do not know anything.<br /><br />I don't think this was a bad book but I did feel cheated with all the stuff I mentioned in my review. So in spite of the fact that I was invested in the story, I can't give it more then two stars.</span>

<div id="review_46440618" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46440618" />
    <a title="Ash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1884487-ash"><img alt="Ash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291356919p2/1884487.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46440618?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash" href="/user/show/1884487-ash">Ash</a>
      </span>

          marked it as attempted-to-read


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312383695" href="/book/show/3521484-cracked-up-to-be">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46440618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17676309577538552984"> I had very high hopes for this book. It had nothing but raving reviews and I was looking forward to reading it. I'm not saying that it disappointed me, but I guess I wasn't as prepared for it as I thought. I knew that it was a fairly raw and somewhat sad book with crude humor and some bad language but I thought I might still be able to get into the book. That I'd be able to finish it.<br/> <br/> Parker is just a sad character. She pushes everyone away by being mean and rude any chance she gets. She doesn</span>
  <span id="freeText17676309577538552984" style="display:none"> I had very high hopes for this book. It had nothing but raving reviews and I was looking forward to reading it. I'm not saying that it disappointed me, but I guess I wasn't as prepared for it as I thought. I knew that it was a fairly raw and somewhat sad book with crude humor and some bad language but I thought I might still be able to get into the book. That I'd be able to finish it.<br /> <br /> Parker is just a sad character. She pushes everyone away by being mean and rude any chance she gets. She doesn't realize that she actually needs the help that people are offering her. I can relate to her in that sense though. It does seem pretty stupid that such big problems can be fixed in such simple ways. I can't see how she's able to be so horrible to the people around her though. It's just selfish that she cares too much about her own feelings of wanting to be alone that she doesn't care if she hurts someone else. You'd think with all the guilt she feels she'd want to stop hurting people. <br /> It was just plain painful seeing her destroy herself and her relationships, and then distance herself from the people who cared about her. The secret that keeps her guilt ridden is a pretty horrible one. I'm not sure if I could ever forgive myself for something like that.<br /> I stopped about halfway through and skipped around until the end. The ending does give a sense of hope that Parker will get better, but I still don't recommend it. It's not because I hated it or because it was bad writing, because it wasn't. There just isn't any point in reading a book that is so sad and depressing when the conclusion doesn't seem to give very much resolution.<br /> <br />If you do decide to read it anyway (who knows, maybe I missed something great in between those couple pages that I skipped completely) then I think I should warn you that this book has sexual content, crude humor, underage drinking (duh) and a good dose of cussing (which we all know is what high school is really like). </span>
  <a data-text-id="17676309577538552984" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('slHyfOr3XY1PvTEvwa+1cXl0nphD/c1SRZp6HW4iJKOaVcZ3th/Ik5mcrnoKlGmdevaax2VonU3QGzQ9U62smg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ymfc5ZV6vOuV8Fjwa+PqT908OPZjvJhzkdI9bc3WF1pKY+juyZIp9UPRx6Wg2Daj3r48qUUpyGwEU3NN8FmfYw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4045910107237224087">Courtney Summers is the bestselling author of several novels, whose career in writing began in 2008, when she was 22. Her work has been released to critical acclaim and multiple starred reviews, received numerous awards and honors including the Edgar Award, the John Spray Mystery Award, the Cybils Award, the Odyssey Award, the Audie Award, and has enjoyed the recognition of many library, state, 'B</span>
  <span id="freeText4045910107237224087" style="display:none">Courtney Summers is the bestselling author of several novels, whose career in writing began in 2008, when she was 22. Her work has been released to critical acclaim and multiple starred reviews, received numerous awards and honors including the Edgar Award, the John Spray Mystery Award, the Cybils Award, the Odyssey Award, the Audie Award, and has enjoyed the recognition of many library, state, 'Best Of' and Readers' Choice lists. Courtney has reviewed for The <em>New York Times</em>, is the founder of #ToTheGirls, a 2015 worldwide trending hashtag, and in 2016, she was named one of <em>Flare</em> Magazine's 60 under 30. She lives and writes in Canada. Her new novel, <em>The Project</em> releases February 2nd, 2021 from Wednesday Books, an imprint of St. Martin's Press. You can follow her on <a href="http://instagram.com/summerscourtney" target="ig" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>, <a href="http://twitter.com/courtney_s" target="twitter" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> and <a href="https://www.facebook.com/CourtneySummersAuthor/" target="fb" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>.</span>
